218 
 
 
 
Specimen after crack propagation over full-height and at the moment of failure and after end of tests 
 
It can be seen from the cracking pattern at the top front face, that the load was applied through 
the webs of the U-profile. The cracks met and merged to propagate as one in the direction of the 
load. 
 
 
 
 
Inspection after test, full-height crack at the back and cracking pattern at the top of the front face 
 
The failure was induced by the out-of-plane buckling of the split-off column that could not 
bear the load after its redistribution due to the local failure at the top that lead to the 
reduction of the cross section.

PO_5B_E20 
Nu = 1438 kN (06.12.2024) 
 
 
 
The first crack occurred at the upper left part of the front face followed by another central crack 
propagating from top towards the middle of the HCSW. The kink at 1081 kN is due to the crack 
propagation and opening of the left crack (See below) that was accompanied by a bang and a 
concrete piece falling off from the upper left corner. 
 
 
 
After reaching the ultimate load, the concrete spalling continued and more and more pieces fell off 
leading to the redistribution of the load (See several kinks in the orange graph above). A splitting 
sound occurred, signaling the crack opening of the central crack. Failure: After more pieces falling 
off, a bang occurred which was accompanied by many pieces falling off including the spalling of a 
bigger pieces from the front face of the specimen.

PO_3A_E55 
Nu = 1007 kN (02.12.2024) 
 
 
 
No kinks occurred during the deformation-driven test until the ultimate load. The load-
deformation behaviour is represented by a continuous graph. A sudden splitting sound and 
propagation of two bigger and a couple of smaller skewed cracks occurred at 1007 kN – the 
ultimate load, followed by concrete pieces falling off from the top.  
 
 
 
The reduction of the cross section and the subsequent redistribution of the load explain the kinks 
in the graph illustrating the load-deformation behaviour after the ultimate load was reached. Finally, 
the crack opened up further, followed by a bang and the in-plane-buckling of the split-off column 
in the transversal direction (last big kink of the dark blue graph).

I ReHoCS: Reuse of hollow core slabs 
 
Example calculation for a residential building 
 
Dead line load of walls (for ground floor) 
 
𝑔2,Q,757 = (𝑛H −1) ∙𝑑Q,=R ∙ℎQ ∙𝛾1 
(A5) 
 
 
nF 
Number of floors: 5 
 
dW,eq 
Equivalent thickness of HCS: 0.13 m ((AHCS = 78.150 mm2)/(bHCS = 600 mm) 
 
hW 
Height of wall: 3 m 
 
γc 
Density of reinforced concrete: 25 kN/m3 
 
The dead load for the ground floor walls gk,walls,tot results as ca. 40 kN/m.  
 
Additional dead load from 
 
Floor slabs (5 storeys): 
 
𝑔2,H,757 = 𝑛H ∙𝑑H ∙𝛾1 ∙𝐿;I 
(A6) 
 
 
nF 
Number of floors: 5 
 
dF 
Thickness of massive floor slab: 0.25 m 
 
γc 
Density of reinforced concrete: 25 kN/m3 
 
LDI 
Draw-in width of load: 6 m 
 
à In total, the floor slabs account for a line load of ca. 190 kN/m. 
 
Additional load on roof and floors:  
 
𝑔2,B,L<< = 𝑔F558 ∙𝐿;I 
(A7) 
 
and 
 
𝑔2,H,L<< = (𝑛H −1) ∙𝑔8455F ∙𝐿;I 
(A8) 
 
 
groof  
5 kN/m2 
 
gfloor 
2,5 kN/m2 
 
LDI 
Draw-in width of load: 6 m 
 
This results as 30 kN/m and 15 kN/m per floor. In total this sums up to a line load of 90 kN/m 
for the ground floor walls. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:243==
 
228 
Imposed load 
 
For roof incl. installations: 5 kN/m2, for other floor slabs 2.7 kN/m2 incl. separation walls. 
 
𝑞2 = (𝑞2,B + 𝑛H ∙𝑞2,H) ∙𝐿;I  
(A9) 
 
 
nF 
Number of floors: 5 
 
qk,R 
Imposed load on roof: 5 kN/m2 
 
 
qk,F 
Imposed load on floors: 2.7 kN/m2 
 
LDI 
Draw-in width of load 
 
Results as ca. 95 kN/m. 
 
Total line load lW,GF,tot for the walls on the groundfloor 
 
𝑙Q,SH,757 = 𝑔2,Q,757 + 𝑔2,H,757 + 𝑔2,B,L<< + 𝑔2,H,L<< + 𝑞2  
(A10) 
 
 
 
gk,W,tot 40 kN/m: Summarized dead line load of walls over 4 storeys 
 
gk,F,tot 190 kN/m: Dead load from 5 floor slabs 
 
gk,add,tot 90 kN/m: Additional dead load on floor slabs and roof 
 
qk 
ca. 100 kN/m: Imposed load   
 
The total line load of 420 kN/m is rounded up to 0.5 MN/m.
